---
title: "12.10 crashes related to Xorg on iMac G3"
date: 2012-11-07
forum: Apple Hardware Users
---

### Post by stlu on 2012-11-07
So I have come into possesion of an iMac G3 with no OS on it. This is the exact model: 
[http://www.everymac.com/systems/apple/imac/specs/imac_se_600.html](http://www.everymac.com/systems/apple/imac/specs/imac_se_600.html)  (I have verified that it was upgraded from 128MB to 512 MB RAM)
 I wanted to see if I could get it running Linux.  I am using it with a standard USB keyboard as opposed to a mac keyboard.

I have come closer to understanding the issue because of a text-based Debian install that only had problems after a graphical environment was installed.


**The problem happens in Debian**
First I tried installing Debian 6.0.6 PPC CD#1, and the first CD doesn't install a graphical environment, which is more of a gift then a nuissance, since it worked fine until I installed Xorg from cd #2.

When I rebooted the Debian system to see if it would work, I noticed that the hard drive, after going quiet from the boot, was making little seeks over and over again, and it sounded like something was loading in a loop.  Also, the caps lock and numlock lights could not be toggled, so the system was nearly fully frozen

So I SSH'ed into the iMac from another pc, and I looked to see what I could find out, and it turned out that the X windowing system was loading and then dying repeatedly.  The details aren't relevant here on Ubuntu forums, but it is worthy of mention that gdm3 and the ATI driver seem to also be crashing repeatedly - or it might just be Xorg forcing them to terminate every time Xorg crashed.


**Trying Lubuntu**
Out of curiousity, I then downloaded *lubuntu-12.10-alternate-powerpc.iso*.  I chose alternate because I was fairly certain that the LiveCD of Lubuntu would encounter the same graphical problems as Debian, and I felt it would be easier to work on the problem from the hard disk, where changes wouldn't be lost on reboot.  Also LXDE is reported to take the least memory compared to XFCE and KDE.

Again, everything text mode was working fine, and the install completed.  On reboot, the "Lubuntu 12.10" splash screen showed for a moment, and then it was black screen just like Debian.  Only Lubuntu doesn't come with SSHD running so I can't get you any log information from it (I will try to set up a separate Debian partition so I can boot it and retrieve log files from the Lubuntu partition, and to paste various xorg.conf files available online)

OH, another important point of frustration: thanks to the Debian install, I found that it is impossible to hit ALT+WindowsKey+[1-6] to get to a TTY, because the console keeps snapping back to TTY7 each time Xorg fires up, so you might be able to get in one or two letters of your username, but it is pointless as long as Xorg keeps taking over your monitor.  On Debian the login prompt showed for a fraction of a second each time I pressed the key combo, while Lubuntu never let me see my TTY1.


[B]Is xorg.conf really the magic answer?

[/B]I have read several posts saying that xorg.conf will fix everything.  But there are a lot of options to set, and I would like to know how to isolate Xorg as the problem.  Because if the open source ATI driver just won't work with this model, I would like to avoid wasting time making hundreds of changes to xorg.conf only to find out that it wasn't the problem in the first place.  How can I confirm that my problem is the same one that is fixable by creating an xorg.conf file?



**EDIT**: I booted with yaboot into single-user mode with "Linux single" and installed openssh-server.

Here is the contents of /var/log/Xorg.0.log for the Lubuntu 12.10 without creating xorg.conf::

_imac3.txt_

This one doesn't match my model, but I tried it anyway. Surprisingly, it worked a bit. I got a black screen with a mouse in the centre. Just a mouse. I was able to move it to all edges of the screen and stuff, no crashing occured. All I need is the REST of the display...

_imac1a.txt_ - It works!  Or it works??

Another one that doesnt match my model.  And I almost didnt' use it because it was for an Italian keyboard layout.  I'm glad I did, because this conf allowed me to see the login manager lightdm, and then login to the DE. 
There was an error, messagebox that popped up, saying that a system error had occured with ... take a guess... Xorg.  Well I reported the error so hopefully the Italians will have a working setup once its fixed...
I would add that opening LXTerminal shocked me with a hideous green background and gray text that was hard to read.

_imac4.txt_

This one also does not match my model, it is for slot loading G3-350MHz models.  Now things are starting to look positive.  The visual came up, and the crash reporting service didn't come up this time.  Also, LXTerminal showed the proper black background.

_imac5.txt_

This file is targeted at the slotloading 400,450 models. Again, its not for my machine, but I'm  trying everything to help anyone with their own G3 machine.
So this also worked, no discolouration on LXTerminal.  Howerver, I found there was some corruption of the characters in LXTerminal, while pressing the Up arrow key to go back to earlier commands.  Looks like the new caracters overlap the existing characters and so sometimes the words were unreadable until iI caused it to refresh.

_imac10.txt_

This one was for a summer 2001 (im assuming the 700MHz model).  It's a bit later then my model, but again, trying everything.  It did load into the Lubuntu desktop, and there was no crash reporting service messages.  This also had some character corruption with the LXTerminal, just like the one before.

_imac11.txt_

This one was actually for my model, though I didn't see it until I got to the bottom of that page.  Thankfully this one worked when the other model-600 files would not.  Also, the corruption in scrolling commands in LXTerminal appear to be gone with this configuration.

[    37.704] (**) Mouseemu virtual mouse: (accel) acceleration profile 0
[    37.705] (**) Mouseemu virtual mouse: (accel) acceleration factor: 2.000
[    37.705] (**) Mouseemu virtual mouse: (accel) acceleration threshold: 4

```

So in conclusion, it does confirm that xorg.conf is a way to make this work.  However the files that were supposed to work, didnt, and the files that weren't for my machine worked.

And just because the Desktop session displays doesn't mean that everything has been fixed - I experienced colour distortions and visual corruption with the little testing I did.

In my opinion, the Troubleshooting guide should have this problem as the FIRST problem to tackle, since I really wasn't sure if this was the right solution for my machine.

[SIZE=1]Someone in the Debian forums make a sarcastic joke that new users would be "joyous" at booting to a text system instead of [SIZE=1]a [SIZE=1]DE[/SIZE][/SIZE].  But I've spent a few hours trying (and failing)to get NetBSD-sgimips onto a Silicon Graphics O2, and with this iM[SIZE=1]ac [/SIZE]I really am joyous to see that black screen with the login prompt!  I am not spoiled, I only want to explore the graphical environment to see if it is possible.[/SIZE]

---

### Post by stlu on 2012-11-07

_imac2.txt_ - [G3 imac slotloader xorg.conf]("http://mac.linux.be/content/g3-imac-slotloader-xorgconf")

This config crashed xorg and brought me to TTY1.  TTY7 had the system startup messages on it.  It is interesting to note that while my machine is a slotloader model, the trayloader confs seem to cause less severe problems then the slotloader confs...

_iMac g3 ppc users dream xorg.conf_ - [Ubuntu Forum thread]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1215154")

Well this may not be a dream xorg.conf, but it did work for my 600MHz machine and Lubuntu 12.10 alternate.  There was no character corruption while scolling through history on LXTerminal either.

### Post by rsavage on 2012-11-08
> 
In my opinion, the Troubleshooting guide should have this problem as the  FIRST problem to tackle, since I really wasn't sure if this was the  right solution for my machine.
Graphics problems is the third in the list []"]https://wiki.ubuntu.com/PowerPCFAQ#Ubuntu_boots_to_a_command_line.2C_hangs_during_boot.2C_or_blank_screen_etc.]("https://wiki.ubuntu.com/PowerPCFAQ#Ubuntu_boots_to_a_command_line.2C_hangs_during_boot.2C_or_blank_screen_etc.) so it is hardly buried.

There is a huge section in the PowerPCFAQ with a separate sub-section for rage 128 cards [https://wiki.ubuntu.com/PowerPCFAQ#ATI_Rage_128_cards](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/PowerPCFAQ#ATI_Rage_128_cards)

In bold writing is the advice to set HorizSync/VertRefresh values. 
```

[B]If you have a G3 iMac then the values you get from the ddcprobe  command are likely to be too restrictive.  Use the values 58-62 and  75-117 instead.

[/B]
```So all the changes you need to make are in the FAQ.

> 
So in conclusion, it does confirm that xorg.conf is a way to make this  work.  However the files that were supposed to work, didnt, and the  files that weren't for my machine worked.
Which is why in the FAQ is says not to use them
```

Sample xorg.files for various machines can be found [here]("http://mac.linux.be/content/xorgconf-files").  These can sometimes save you reading the documentation, but some of  them are not the best setup (that's a polite way of putting it!.....and  if you still haven't taken the hint.....you are recommended *not* to use them or look at them unless you are really stuck).

```12.10 uses EXA for the first time so you may have to work out a few more things than what is documented currently.  The FAQ and KnownIssues pages are community documents so if you are unhappy with them you are free to edit them yourself.

---
